Spited by the furtrap again!<br /><br />This trimmer is an invaluable tool of the bearded male who shares a sink with a female.   11. Pros:<br />+ Lithium-Ion battery holds a charge longer<br />+ International-voltage charger<br />+ Fine-grained and more secure height adjustment<br /><br />Cons:<br />- Swing-open door for hair removal a pain<br />- No narrow-blade accessory for mustaches<br />- No carrying case<br />- Somewhat wimpy vacuum<br /><br />For the past two and a half years, I have been using the [[ASIN:B000FEF1V4 Philips Norelco T980 Turbo Vacuum Trimmer]], which is an earlier generation of the Qt4050. I've been generally satisfied with the T980, except that its NiCd battery won't hold a charge anymore. The Qt4050 has a big advantage in that it uses a Lithium-Ion battery, rare in products of this nature, though I expect it will become more common in the future. Li-Ion batteries last longer between charges and don't degrade as quickly as NiCd or NiMH batteries do. I also like that the Qt4050 includes a universal-voltage AC charger, unlike the T980 which was US voltage only.<br /><br />Another advantage of the newer model is the height adjustment - there are more settings available and the setting is clearly indicated in inches and millimeters, whereas the T980 just had a 1-10 numbered dial. The T980's adjustment dial would sometimes get moved, especially if something pushed on the trimming comb (such as if it was packed for travel.) The newer design seems to be more resistant to that.<br /><br />One change I do not care for is how one empties the vacuumed hair. On the T980, there was a generously-sized cup that just pulled out and you could tap over a wastebasket. The new model has a swing-out door with a rather difficult-to-open catch. The hair chamber is small, and has crevices that catch hair. One has to use the supplied brush to get most of the hair out, but some will remain nonetheless. The new one also seems to collect more hair in and around the comb than the old one.<br /><br />The actual trimming function for the Qt4050 is fine, and is pretty much the same as the T980 - no surprise because the blade and comb design is identical. I found I could even swap in the narrow mustache blade from the T980 - the 4050 doesn't include one and I consider this a serious omission for something claiming to be a mustache trimmer. I use the trimmer for my beard and mustache only, not elsewhere on the body.<br /><br />The vacuum works reasonably well - perhaps the \\"turbo\\" motor of the higher priced [[ASIN:B003U8ESI4 Philips Norelco Qt4070/41 Turbo Vacuum Beard, Stubble and Moustach Trimmer Pro]] would be stronger.<br /><br />When using the trimmer without the comb - as one would do for trimming the neck or sideburns, the 4050 lacks the sliding gate that adjusts better for angle that the T980 had, though I'm unsure if this makes a difference in real use.<br /><br />The T980 included a very nice carrying pouch for travel - no such thing for the Qt4050.<br /><br />Since the T980 is still available from Amazon (as of this writing), I'd tend to recommend it over the Qt4050 if it weren't for the NiCd battery issue. However, the battery may not be a deal-killer for most people and both trimmers can be used on AC power even if the battery is dead (you'd be astonished at how many similar products can't be run on AC.) The Qt4050 is by no means a bad product - it's better than those from other manufacturers I have used (and that's quite a few.) It's just disappointing in comparison to its predecessor.<br /><br />Edit: March 23, 2011<br />The T980 is no longer available from Amazon or really anywhere else. Too bad. I have been using the Qt4050 regularly and, other than the poorer vacuum performance, it works ok. I've managed to come to terms with the door over the hair collection chamber and learned to stop and clean it out more often. I do like that I can go a much longer time between charges. (Note that with a Li-Ion battery, it will last longest if you keep it \\"topped up\\", unlike NiCd batteries that prefer being deep-discharged.) If you're considering the Qt4050, maybe spring for the Qt4070 with its more powerful motor. (I have not tried that model, however, and its reviews are decidedly mixed.)<br /><br />In our household, we have a saying that \\"they 'new-and-improved' it\\", meaning that it was made worse than the old model. In some ways that applies to the Qt4050. Who knows - if I had the Qt4070 I might feel differently about it, as the poorer hair collection is really my major gripe compared to the T980.<br /><br />Edit: May 22, 2011<br />Remember when I wrote about the \\"fiddly\\" door over the clipped hair compartment? Now it's more so - the small plastic tab that serves as a latch broke off the door, so it no longer stays shut. I now have to remember to keep my finger on it to keep it from swinging open while in use.r, and its reviews are decidedly mixed.) In our household, we have a saying that \\"they 'new-and-improved' it\\", meaning that it was made worse than the old model. In some ways that applies to the Qt4050. Who knows - if I had the Qt4070 I might feel differently about it, as the poorer hair collection is really my major gripe compared to the T980. Edit: May 22, 2011 Remember when I wrote about the \\"fiddly\\" door over the clipped hair compartment? Now it's more so - the small plastic tab that serves as a latch broke off the door, so it no longer stays shut. I now have to remember to keep my finger on it to keep it from swinging open while in use.
  12. This Norelco beard trimmer is ergonomically shaped and rubberized. It feels lightweight yet sturdy. The blade height adjustment control is a bit unusual, however. The control is located in the middle of the trimmer and is shaped like the dial of a deodorant stick. You twist it to one direction to raise the blade head and twist in the opposite direction to lower it.<br /><br />The main problem I have with it is the vacuum feature. It's pretty useless. There's a small motor inside the housing that sucks air in. It's more like a faint breeze than a vacuum. Hair collects in a small windowed compartment that has to be emptied frequently. It owes the collecting ability more to gravity than vacuum suction.<br /><br />This product is good for grooming beards, but don't count on the vacuum doing its job very well. You're probably going still going to have to wipe up stray hairs from your sink. I had quite an amount of beard trimmings to clean up trimming my 1/2\\" beard. On a positive note, battery retention is excellent and it holds its charge for several months.

The trimmer is light weight and feels good in your hand; it smoothly follow the contours of your face. It has 18 different length settings, which I find particularly useful. Each setting is reached by simply rotating a wheel that clicks into place at each length. Given these clicks, there is no guess work as to which length setting you are on. The vacuum compartment door is clear, so you know when it's time to empty the razor. While the design of this trimmer ranks high, parts of its execution are lacking. The obvious shortcoming for me is the vacuum. I find it ineffective. For every hair the trimmer collects, it seems to spill one into the sink. So, great, I still have to clean out my sink while also having to clean out the trimmer's vacuum compartment. Philips has the right idea by adding a vacuum, but there is still work to be done in the R & D department before this feature becomes a selling point. The trimmer has also clogged a couple of times when I've trimmed off any significant amount of hair. I know most beard trimmers occasionally clog, but other Norelco products I've used haven't had this problem. Finally, this trimmer is not ideal for use on a mustache. Unless you remove the guard, it can be difficult to maneuver the blade around your upper lip. And, if you have to remove the guard, it defeats the purpose of having a trimmer in the first place. The bottom line is that this is a sturdy product that is better than a lot of options out there right now, but it isn't overly impressive by Norelco standards.

  134. The Philips Norelco Vacuum Beard Trimmer Plus is a great litter trimmer. It works well, feels solid and comfortable in the hand, and keeps your sink mostly free from trimmed hairs.<br /><br />The trimmer is a decent size (about the size of a TV remote control) and is shaped like an ice cream cone. It is put together well, is light in weight, and has a rubberized grip on the back. There is a spinning dial that you use to adjust the height of the cutting comb, which in turn determines the length of your beard. The dial clicks into place very firmly so you don't have to worry about it moving if you press too hard while trimming. The comb adjusts from 18mm to 1mm in cutting length. Additionally you can pull off the comb and use the blades to clean up the edges on your beard. There is a single power button on the front and that pretty much does it for controls. It's very simple to use.<br /><br />Included with the trimmer is a compact charger that is nicely done as well, with a little rubber grip. On the front of the trimmer, below the power button, is a battery light that indicates when the battery is low, when the battery is charging, and when it is done charging.<br /><br />The trimmer has a built in vacuum system that is supposed to suck the cut hairs into a chamber so they don't just fall into the bathroom sink. The vacuum works for the most part but there are always a few stray hairs that make it to the sink. When the time comes to clean out the trimmer you just pull open the little door on the front and dump out the hair. It works well, but an older Norelco vacuum trimmer I have has a little drawer that you pull out. That system works a bit better than this new one, as it is a bit less cumbersome and messy. Lastly, you can also pull off the cutting comb, remove part of the blade assembly, and clean under there, but that does not need to be done often.<br /><br />In use the trimmer is smooth. It never snags or feels painful, and there's a spring-loaded part on the back of the comb that follows the contours of your face. Volume wise, it's not much louder than a regular electric shaver.<br /><br />The only negative about the trimmer I have is that it takes 8 hours to fully charge the battery, granted it lasts a couple of weeks between charges, but 8 hours is a bit longer than ideal. However, you can use it while it is plugged in, so if you don't have time to wait for a complete charge.<br /><br />All in all... a terrific beard trimmer that prevents a mess of hair from landing in your sink.s the contours of your face. Volume wise, it's not much louder than a regular electric shaver. The only negative about the trimmer I have is that it takes 8 hours to fully charge the battery, granted it lasts a couple of weeks between charges, but 8 hours is a bit longer than ideal. It has a clear plastic cover over a chamber for trimmed hair to be deposited by a built in vacuum device. The blades cut a 1 1/4 inch path, wide enough for efficiency in cutting broad areas of the cheeks and neck yet narrow enough to trim mustaches and sideburns. Blades and rechargeable battery are replaceable by the owner.<br /><br />I have worn a beard most of the time for many years, and have kept it short, medium, and long to fit the occasion. I always determined length in the past with an electric barber razor with a few available attachments. The built in beard length determiner of the Norelco is very useful. Turning a wheel to the desired setting in the body of the trimmer guarantees consistent length. Trimming cleanly without putting down newspapers to collect cut hair is a real advantage offered by the vacuum and hair collection chamber.<br /><br />This is an excellent beard trimmer, and the owner will not have to allow a beard to grow beyond desired limits because of the hassle of setting up a cutting session. The first two models (5100 and 9100) have dual side trimmers that can trim your beard or be turned to trim the beard edge. The 4050 lacks the edge trimmer but has a built-in vacuum to capture cut whiskers. The 9100 model has a built-in laser that is supposed to be helpful when trimming the edge.<br /><br />Both the 5100 and 9100 models are relatively quiet whereas the 4050 is quite noisy. All three products trim beards equally well. The 4050 vacuum system works quite well and is a feature that my wife appreciates very much as there are no (or very few) loose hairs left over from the trim. The other two products leave hair detritus in the bathroom sink and surrounding area. This is the beard trimmer that I will continue to use.<br /><br />I have to say, though, that the laser gizmo on the 9100 model is fun to use. You remove the guide, press down on a button, and the laser pops up and casts a red line across your face or wherever else you point it. I found it useless for actually guiding the trimming, but it is fun to play with in a transformer sort of way.
